{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01TVFcoTL6SWe4ZXupqa11Jd","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01FPsbiCrfnURtuLE6TvQ92H","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe QueueSet subsystem implements **Fair Queuing for Server Requests (FQSR)**, a specialized fair-queuing algorithm that multiplexes concurrent API server requests across priority levels. It provides weighted fairness guarantees through virtual time scheduling, shuffle-sharded queue assignment, and adaptive dispatch based on estimated work (seat-seconds). This document traces the end-to-end control flow, dissects the fairness algorithm, and discusses operational tradeoffs.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### 1.1 Purpose\n\nThe QueueSet is the **execution scheduling engine** of API Priority and Fairness (APF). It sits between the APF filter (which classifies requests) and the main request handler (which executes them). Its role:\n\n- **Admission control**: Reject or queue requests when concurrency limits are exceeded\n- **Fair dispatch**: Select which queued request executes next, ensuring:\n  - Proportional fairness among flows (via virtual time)\n  - Starvation prevention (via round-robin queue selection)\n  - Work-aware scheduling (via seat-seconds, not just request count)\n- **Concurrency accounting**: Track occupied \"seats\" (a logical concurrency unit) across phases of request execution\n\n### 1.2 Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n- **APF Controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`): Provides `QueuingConfig` (desired number of queues, queue length limit, hand size for shuffle sharding) and `DispatchingConfig` (concurrency limit)\n- **Request classifiers**: Extract flow distinguisher and match requests to priority levels\n- **Work estimators** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go`): Estimate request width (initial seats, final seats, additional latency) based on request type and payload size\n\n**Downstream dependencies:**\n- **HTTP handler**: Calls `StartRequest()`, then `req.Finish()` when done\n- **Metrics subsystem** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics/`): Observes request counts, seat occupancy, dispatch latencies, rejections\n- **Event clock** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/`): Provides virtual time ticking and delayed event scheduling\n\n### 1.3 Key Data Dependencies\n\n- **WorkEstimate**: Carries `InitialSeats` (concurrency during main phase), `FinalSeats` (reserved after execution), and `AdditionalLatency` (padding duration)\n- **SeatSeconds**: Fixed-point representation of work = seats × duration, with 1e8 internal scale factor\n- **QueuingConfig**: Encodes desired number of queues (0 = bypass queueing, negative = exempt), queue length limit, shuffle-sharding hand size\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Types\n\n#### `queueSet` (queueset.go:85–167)\nThe main orchestrator. Fields include:\n- **`queues []*queue`**: Array of FIFO queues, allocated per shuffle-sharded flow\n- **`currentR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Global virtual time progress meter (R from fair queuing)\n- **`lock sync.Mutex`**: Protects all mutable state\n- **`totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`**: Aggregate seat occupancy\n- **`totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`**: Request counts for metrics\n- **`dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig`**: Concurrency limits and seat accounting denominators\n- **`promiseFactory`**: Creates decision promises (deferred-write channels for async dispatch decisions)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Initial request ingress and rejection (via `StartRequest()`)\n- Virtual time progression and epoch management\n- Dispatch loop orchestration\n- Request completion tracking and seat release\n\n#### `queue` (types.go:93–110)\nPer-flow-distinguisher queue. Fields:\n- **`requestsWaiting fifo`**: Ordered list of queued requests\n- **`requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]`**: Executing requests from this queue (for seat tracking)\n- **`nextDispatchR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Virtual finish time of next dispatch from this queue\n- **`seatsInUse int`**: Occupied seats in this queue\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- FIFO ordering of requests awaiting dispatch\n- Virtual time tracking per queue (anti-windup mechanism)\n\n#### `request` (types.go:33–83)\nRequest wrapper with scheduling metadata. Fields:\n- **`decision promise.WriteOnce`**: Deferred decision (execute/cancel)\n- **`arrivalTime`, `startTime`**: Real timestamps for latency metrics\n- **`arrivalR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Virtual time at arrival\n- **`workEstimate completedWorkEstimate`**: Computed total work (initial + final)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Carries request context and work estimate\n- Defers dispatch decision via promise pattern (allows async decision-setting under lock, decision-reading without lock)\n\n#### `requestFIFO` (fifo_list.go:71–156)\nLinked-list FIFO with aggregate statistics. Methods:\n- **`Enqueue(req)`**: Returns `removeFromFIFOFunc` for O(1) removal\n- **`QueueSum()`**: Returns aggregated `InitialSeatsSum`, `MaxSeatsSum`, `TotalWorkSum`\n- **`Walk(func)`**: Iterates without copying (permits removal during iteration)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- O(1) enqueue/dequeue/remove operations\n- Maintains running sums of seated widths for shuffle-sharding decisions\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Request Arrival: `StartRequest()` (queueset.go:308–356)\n\n```\n┌─ StartRequest(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, ...)\n│\n├─ Step 0: Check if queueing is bypassed\n│  │  (DesiredNumQueues < 1 → concurrency-only mode)\n│  │\n│  ├─ If queues disabled:\n│  │  └─ Call canAccommodateSeatsLocked(workEstimate.MaxSeats)\n│  │     ├─ If yes: dispatchSansQueueLocked() → return request (immediate exec)\n│  │     └─ If no: increment totRequestsRejected, return (nil, isIdleLocked)\n│  │\n│  └─ If queues enabled: proceed to Step 1\n│\n├─ Step 1: Shuffle-shard and enqueue\n│  │\n│  ├─ shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()\n│  │  │\n│  │  ├─ Call shuffleShardLocked(hashValue)\n│  │  │  │  Uses dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue) to get candidate queues\n│  │  │  │  Selects queue with minimum TotalWorkSum (load-balanced assignment)\n│  │  │  │\n│  │  │  └─ Return queue index\n│  │  │\n│  │  ├─ Create request object with:\n│  │  │  ├─ arrivalTime ← clock.Now()\n│  │  │  ├─ arrivalR ← currentR (current virtual time)\n│  │  │  ├─ decision ← promiseFactory(nil) [decision not yet set]\n│  │  │  └─ workEstimate ← completeWorkEstimate(workEstimate)\n│  │  │\n│  │  ├─ Call rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n│  │  │  │\n│  │  │  ├─ If totSeatsInUse >= concurrencyLimit AND queueLength >= queueLengthLimit:\n│  │  │  │  └─ REJECT (return false)\n│  │  │  │\n│  │  │  └─ Else: enqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n│  │  │     ├─ If queue empty: queue.nextDispatchR ← currentR (initialize virtual start)\n│  │  │     ├─ queue.requestsWaiting.Enqueue(request)\n│  │  │     ├─ totRequestsWaiting++, totSeatsWaiting += request.MaxSeats()\n│  │  │     └─ Metrics: AddRequestsInQueues, AddSeatsInQueues\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ If rejected: return nil\n│  │\n│  └─ If enqueued: proceed to Step 2\n│\n├─ Step 2: Immediate dispatch as much as possible\n│  │\n│  └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n│     │  While totRequestsWaiting > 0 AND totSeatsInUse < concurrencyLimit:\n│     │    └─ dispatchLocked() (see Section 3.2)\n│     │\n│     └─ Executes requests from queues until concurrency limit or no queued requests\n│\n└─ Return (request, false)\n   │  If request is nil: caller should reject\n   │  If request is non-nil: caller must call request.Finish() when done\n```\n\n### 3.2 Dispatch: `dispatchLocked()` and Fair Queue Selection (queueset.go:695–743)\n\nFair Queuing uses **virtual time** to achieve fairness. Key insight: dispatch the request whose virtual *finish time* is earliest, ensuring proportional service allocation.\n\n```\n┌─ dispatchLocked()\n│\n├─ findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n│  │\n│  ├─ Iterate round-robin through queues\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ For each queue with waiting requests:\n│  │     │\n│  │     ├─ Peek oldest request\n│  │     │\n│  │     ├─ Compute currentVirtualFinish:\n│  │     │  │  = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n│  │     │  │\n│  │     │  │  Where totalWork = InitialSeats×EstimatedServiceDuration\n│  │     │  │                     + FinalSeats×AdditionalLatency\n│  │     │  │\n│  │     │  └─ If currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish:\n│  │     │     └─ Record this queue as best candidate\n│  │     │\n│  │     └─ Also track virtual dispatch start (nextDispatchR - estimatedWorkInProgress)\n│  │        for metrics\n│  │\n│  ├─ Check canAccommodateSeatsLocked(selectedRequest.MaxSeats)\n│  │  │\n│  │  ├─ If seats exceed ConcurrencyLimit AND executingRequests > 0:\n│  │  │  │  CANNOT dispatch yet (must wait for current requests to finish)\n│  │  │  │\n│  │  │  └─ Return (nil, nil) → caller stops dispatching\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ If can accommodate: dequeue from requestsWaiting\n│  │\n│  ├─ Adjust final seats if they exceed concurrency limit\n│  │  │  (preserve total work by adjusting additional latency)\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ Update round-robin index to start from selected queue next time\n│  │\n│  └─ Return (selectedQueue, selectedRequest)\n│\n├─ Remove request from waiting list:\n│  │  ├─ totRequestsWaiting--, totSeatsWaiting -= request.MaxSeats()\n│  │  ├─ Metrics: AddRequestsInQueues(-1), AddSeatsInQueues(-maxSeats)\n│  │  └─ request.NoteQueued(false)\n│  │\n│  └─ defer boundNextDispatchLocked(queue) [anti-windup; see 3.5]\n│\n├─ Set dispatch decision:\n│  │\n│  └─ If request.decision.Set(decisionExecute) succeeds:\n│     │  (decision promise was unfulfilled; now fulfilled)\n│     │\n│     ├─ Move from waiting to executing:\n│     │  ├─ request.startTime ← clock.Now()\n│     │  ├─ queue.requestsExecuting.Insert(request)\n│     │  ├─ queue.seatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n│     │  ├─ totRequestsExecuting++, totSeatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n│     │  └─ Metrics: AddRequestsExecuting(+1), AddSeatConcurrencyInUse(+seats)\n│     │\n│     ├─ Advance virtual finish time:\n│     │  │\n│     │  └─ queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n│     │     │  \"Cost\" of this request in virtual time\n│     │     │  Larger work → larger virtual advance → less priority to future requests\n│     │     │\n│     │     └─ Other queues see this queue recede in virtual time\n│     │\n│     └─ Return true (dispatch succeeded)\n│\n└─ Return false (if decision.Set failed or no queue candidate)\n   │  Caller will retry this request once another finishes\n   │\n   └─ (Can only happen if request's context was canceled before dispatch)\n```\n\n### 3.3 Virtual Time Progression: `syncTimeLocked()` (queueset.go:465–522)\n\nVirtual time advances proportionally to concurrency limits and active queue load:\n\n```\n┌─ syncTimeLocked(ctx)\n│\n├─ Measure elapsed real time:\n│  │  realNow := clock.Now()\n│  │  timeSinceLast := realNow - lastRealTime\n│  │\n│  └─ lastRealTime ← realNow\n│\n├─ Compute virtual time advancement rate:\n│  │\n│  └─ getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()\n│     │\n│     ├─ activeQueues ← count of non-empty queues\n│     │\n│     ├─ seatsRequested ← ∑(queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.MaxSeatsSum)\n│     │\n│     ├─ If activeQueues == 0:\n│     │  │  return 0 (no advancement while idle)\n│     │  │\n│     │  └─ No virtual time consumption\n│     │\n│     └─ Else:\n│        return min(seatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n│        │\n│        │  Each active queue \"consumes\" an equal share of concurrency\n│        │  Unmet demand (seatsRequested > limit) means queues share fairly\n│        │  Unmet demand (seatsRequested < limit) means virtual time = real time\n│\n├─ Advance global progress meter:\n│  │\n│  └─ currentR += SeatsTimesDuration(ratio, timeSinceLast)\n│     │  Converts: (seats/queue) × (elapsed time) → seat-seconds\n│     │  Uses fixed-point SeatSeconds (scale = 1e8)\n│\n└─ If currentR >= highR (overflow threshold):\n   │\n   └─ advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n      │  Decrement currentR and all queue.nextDispatchR by rDecrement (2^63)\n      │  Prevents uint64 overflow\n      │  Idempotent for queues that become empty\n      │\n      └─ [See Section 3.5 for anti-windup implications]\n```\n\n**Key insight:** Virtual time rate is `(fair share of concurrency) / (queue count)`. If 4 queues compete for 100-seat limit, each queue \"time\" advances at 25 seats/sec in real time, regardless of actual demand. This provides proportional fairness.\n\n### 3.4 Request Completion: `finishRequestLocked()` (queueset.go:863–943)\n\n```\n┌─ finishRequestLocked(req)\n│\n├─ Update counters:\n│  │  ├─ totRequestsExecuting--\n│  │  ├─ Metrics: AddRequestsExecuting(-1)\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ actualServiceDuration := now - req.startTime\n│\n├─ Determine seat release timing:\n│  │\n│  └─ If AdditionalLatency <= 0:\n│     │  Release all seats immediately\n│     │\n│     └─ releaseSeatsLocked():\n│        ├─ totSeatsInUse -= req.MaxSeats()\n│        ├─ req.queue.seatsInUse -= req.MaxSeats()\n│        ├─ Metrics: AddSeatConcurrencyInUse(-seats)\n│        └─ Call removeQueueIfEmptyLocked() [queue housekeeping]\n│\n│  Else:\n│     │\n│     ├─ Release InitialSeats immediately\n│     │\n│     ├─ Schedule deferred release of FinalSeats after AdditionalLatency\n│     │  │  via clock.EventAfterDuration(func() { releaseSeatsLocked() }, AdditionalLatency)\n│     │  │\n│     │  └─ Client perceives no latency; seats held invisibly in background\n│     │\n│     └─ Post-release: dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n│\n├─ Adjust queue's virtual start time (anti-windup):\n│  │\n│  └─ If req was dispatched from a queue:\n│     │\n│     └─ queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(req.InitialSeats,\n│        EstimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n│        │\n│        │  Rationale:\n│        │  - Estimated cost: initialSeats × estimatedServiceDuration\n│        │  - Actual cost: initialSeats × actualServiceDuration\n│        │  - Difference: credit back to queue if actual < estimated\n│        │\n│        └─ Reduces queue's virtual start time → increases dispatch priority\n│\n└─ Remove request from queue:\n   │\n   ├─ If queued: queue.requestsExecuting.Delete(req)\n   │\n   └─ If not queued (concurrency-only mode):\n      └─ requestsExecutingSet.Delete(req)\n```\n\n### 3.5 Anti-Windup: `boundNextDispatchLocked()` (queueset.go:952–964)\n\n**Problem:** A queue that cannot use all its allocated concurrency (e.g., bursty single-stream) accumulates a decreasing virtual start time (its `nextDispatchR`), gaining unfair priority over busier queues. The anti-windup bounds this:\n\n```\n┌─ boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n│\n├─ If queue is now empty: return (no action needed)\n│\n├─ Peek oldest waiting request:\n│  │  oldestReqFromMinQueue := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n│  │\n│  └─ virtualStartBound := oldestReqFromMinQueue.arrivalR\n│     │  (request cannot start before it arrives)\n│\n└─ If queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound:\n   │\n   ├─ queue.nextDispatchR ← virtualStartBound\n   │\n   └─ Log: \"AntiWindup tweaked queue\" with delta\n      │\n      └─ Prevents dispatch before arrival\n```\n\n**Rationale:** If a queue is idle (no requests), its virtual time would advance unbounded. When a new request arrives, we clamp the queue's virtual start ≥ arrival time. This prevents \"catching up\" too much.\n\n### 3.6 Request Waiting and Decision: `request.wait()` (queueset.go:397–441)\n\n```\n┌─ req.wait() [called by req.Finish() to get dispatch decision]\n│\n├─ Fetch decision promise:\n│  │  decisionAny := req.decision.Get()\n│  │  │  Blocks until decision is fulfilled (by dispatchLocked or timeout)\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ Lock queueset and sync virtual time\n│\n├─ If decision == decisionExecute:\n│  │  return (true, false)  ← execute the request\n│  │\n│  └─ Caller's execFn() will run immediately\n│\n├─ Else (decision == decisionCancel, due to context timeout/cancel):\n│  │\n│  ├─ Remove request from queue:\n│  │  │  queue.requestsWaiting.Length()--\n│  │  │  totSeatsWaiting -= req.MaxSeats()\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ Metrics: AddReject(..., \"time-out\")\n│  │\n│  └─ return (false, isIdleLocked())  ← request was rejected (timed out)\n│\n└─ Note: Cannot call wait() twice on same request (enforced)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Fairness Algorithm Details\n\n### 4.1 Fair Queuing Foundations\n\nThe QueueSet implements a variant of **Weighted Fair Queuing (WFQ)**. The key idea:\n\n1. **Virtual Time (R):** A monotonically increasing counter measuring work allocated\n2. **Virtual Start/Finish:** Each request has a virtual arrival time (`arrivalR`) and virtual finish time (`arrivalR + totalWork`)\n3. **Selection Rule:** Always dispatch the request with minimum virtual finish time\n4. **Guarantee:** Over long timescales, each flow receives service proportional to its demand (up to fair share)\n\n**Example:**\n- Request A: work = 10 seat-seconds, arrives at R=0 → finishes at R=10\n- Request B: work = 20 seat-seconds, arrives at R=0 → finishes at R=20\n- Dispatch order: A (finish@10), then B (finish@20)\n- If another A arrives at R=10: A2 finishes at R=20 (same as B)\n- Fair: both flows receive equal service time\n\n### 4.2 Virtual Time Rate Adaptation\n\nInstead of fixed-weight fair queuing, the QueueSet uses **dynamic virtual time progression** based on concurrency limits and load:\n\n```\nvirtual_time_rate = min(seatsRequested, concurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\n**Implications:**\n\n| Scenario | seatsRequested | activeQueues | Rate per Queue |\n|----------|----------------|--------------|----------------|\n| 4 queues, 100 seats | 100 | 4 | 25 seats/sec |\n| 4 queues, 40 seats | 40 | 4 | 10 seats/sec |\n| 4 queues, 200 seats | 200 | 4 | 25 seats/sec (clamped) |\n| 2 queues, 100 seats | 100 | 2 | 50 seats/sec |\n\n**Effect:** Queues with low demand don't slow down others. Queues sharing the limit get equal virtual time.\n\n### 4.3 Work Estimation and Seat-Seconds\n\nWork is measured in **seat-seconds**, a two-phase model:\n\n```\ntotalWork = InitialSeats × EstimatedServiceDuration\n          + FinalSeats × AdditionalLatency\n\nExample:\n  ListRequest with 1000 objects\n  InitialSeats=3, EstimatedServiceDuration=3ms → 9ms-seats\n  FinalSeats=1, AdditionalLatency=0 → 0ms-seats\n  Total work = 9 ms-seats\n```\n\n**Why two phases?**\n- **Initial phase:** Request actively uses concurrency (network send, compute)\n- **Final phase:** Minimal active use; seats held for flow completion guarantees (e.g., TCP RST handling)\n\n### 4.4 Shuffle Sharding: Load Balancing Among Queues\n\nShuffle sharding solves a crucial problem: **head-of-line blocking**. Without it, a single slow request from flow X blocks all other requests from X.\n\n**Algorithm** (shuffleShardLocked, queueset.go:583–612):\n\n```\n1. dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, handSize)\n   │  Input: flow's hash, desired hand size (e.g., 8)\n   │  Output: array of queue indices (e.g., [3, 7, 1, 5, 2, 8, 0, 4])\n   │\n   │  Ensures: different flows get different hands, but hands overlap\n   │           (reduces collision probability vs. simple hash mod)\n\n2. Iterate through hand, selecting queue with minimum TotalWorkSum\n   │  offset := enqueues % handSize  (round-robin offset for fairness)\n   │  For i = 0 to handSize-1:\n   │    queueIdx := hand[(offset + i) % handSize]\n   │    if queueSum[queueIdx].TotalWorkSum < minQueueWorkSum:\n   │      bestQueueIdx ← queueIdx\n\n3. Enqueue into bestQueueIdx\n\nOutcome:\n  - Same flow always gets queued to one of its hand's queues\n  - Requests from different flows spread across queues\n  - Load balancing: pick least-loaded queue from hand\n  - Starvation prevention: offset ensures round-robin fairness among hand members\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Shuffle sharding trades determinism for fairness. A flow may experience variable queueing if its hand happens to be congested.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Overflow Management\n\n**Problem:** Virtual time `R` is a `uint64`. After ~584 CPU-years of continuous operation, it overflows.\n\n**Solution:** Epoch advancement (advanceEpoch, queueset.go:492–522)\n\n```\nTrigger: currentR >= highR (where highR = 2^63 + 2^62)\n\nAction:\n  1. Subtract rDecrement (2^63) from:\n     - currentR\n     - All queue.nextDispatchR\n     - All request.arrivalR (for queued requests)\n\n  2. Log the event with old/new values and integrity check\n\nRationale:\n  - Preserves relative ordering (A - C == (A-D) - (C-D))\n  - Resets counter, extending lifetime to another ~584 years\n  - Idempotent for empty queues (nextDispatchR → 0 if queue unused)\n```\n\n**Risk:** If any adjustment underflows (detected and logged), fairness metrics become unreliable, but scheduling continues.\n\n### 5.2 Seat Accommodation and Borrowing Limits\n\n**Problem:** A request may require more seats than the concurrency limit.\n\n**Handling** (canAccommodateSeatsLocked, queueset.go:748–769):\n\n```\nCase 1: DesiredNumQueues < 0 (exempt from limitation)\n  → Always return true (admit request immediately)\n\nCase 2: RequestSeats > ConcurrencyLimit\n  → If totRequestsExecuting == 0: admit (allow one to start)\n  → Else: reject (wait for current requests to finish)\n\nCase 3: RequestSeats + TotSeatsInUse <= ConcurrencyLimit\n  → Admit (sufficient capacity)\n\nCase 4: RequestSeats + TotSeatsInUse > ConcurrencyLimit\n  → Reject (insufficient capacity, must wait)\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Case 2 allows a single request to exceed the limit, but prevents cascading overflow. This violates strict concurrency control but ensures liveness.\n\n### 5.3 Virtual Dispatch Start (Anti-Windup) Limitations\n\n**Problem:** A queue that alternates between idle and active can accumulate a very early `nextDispatchR`, gaining unfair priority.\n\n**Partial mitigation:** boundNextDispatchLocked bounds `nextDispatchR ≥ oldestWaitingRequest.arrivalR`.\n\n**Limitation:** This bound is conservative. If a queue is idle for 1 hour, then receives a request, its virtual start is bumped to the current virtual time, but by then global virtual time has advanced ~10^6 seat-seconds. The queue may have gained priority unfairly.\n\n**Why not fully resync?** Setting `nextDispatchR = currentR` for each idle queue would be too aggressive, allowing \"fresh\" queues to cut in line.\n\n### 5.4 Queue Attrition and Configuration Changes\n\n**Problem:** If desired number of queues decreases, we can't immediately remove occupied queues.\n\n**Handling** (setConfiguration, queueset.go:254–287):\n\n```\nIf DesiredNumQueues decreases from 10 to 5:\n  1. Do not remove extra queues immediately\n  2. Only remove queues when they become empty (attrition)\n  3. Other queue parameters (QueueLengthLimit) frozen while removing queues\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Transient over-provisioning until queues drain. Memory impact is bounded by queue count (each queue is ~200 bytes) and request count.\n\n### 5.5 Queue Length Limits and Rejection\n\n**Rejection criteria** (rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked, queueset.go:618–629):\n\n```\nReject if:\n  totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND\n  curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit\n\nRationale:\n  - Prevent unbounded queue growth (memory DOS)\n  - Allow queueing when concurrency is available (latency isolation)\n  - Admit if either constraint has room\n```\n\n**Problem:** This is an AND condition, not OR. If concurrency limit is hit but queue is short, request is admitted. If queue is full but concurrency available, request is admitted. Only when both are maxed is it rejected.\n\n**Justification:** Reduces unfair rejection during transient overload.\n\n### 5.6 Estimation Error and Service Time Feedback\n\n**Problem:** `EstimatedServiceDuration` is fixed (default 3ms) per queueset. Actual service times vary widely.\n\n**Feedback mechanism** (finishRequestLocked, queueset.go:937–938):\n\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(req.InitialSeats,\n                                           estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n```\n\n**Effect:** If actual < estimated, queue's virtual start decreases (gains priority). If actual > estimated, increases (loses priority).\n\n**Limitation:** Feedback is local to queue; a flow's error doesn't propagate to other queues in the hand. Flow-wide fairness can degrade if one queue overestimates.\n\n### 5.7 Metrics Observation Lag\n\n**Race:** Metrics are updated under lock, but observed external to lock. Between observation and action, state may change.\n\n**Accepted:** This is inherent to sampling metrics. APF clients should not act on single observations.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 6.1 Promise Factory (queueset.go:47–54)\n\nThe dispatch decision is encapsulated in a `promise.WriteOnce` (write-once channel with context cancellation).\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n\nordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory returns promise.NewWriteOnce\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Replace with custom promise implementation for:\n- Custom cancellation behavior (e.g., explicit ack before canceling)\n- Observability (log all decisions)\n- Testing (deterministic decision injection)\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect promise semantics can cause:\n- Deadlock if Set blocks\n- Data races if not thread-safe\n- Request leaks if decision never set\n\n### 6.2 Clock and Virtual Time Control (eventclock.Interface)\n\nQueueSet accepts an `eventclock.Interface` for time operations:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n  Now() time.Time\n  EventAfterDuration(func(time.Time), time.Duration)\n  ...\n}\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Inject custom clock for:\n- **Testing:** Mock time, fast-forward virtual time\n- **Simulation:** Custom virtual time rates\n- **Observability:** Instrument all time-related decisions\n\n**Risk:**\n- Incorrect `EventAfterDuration` timing → seat leaks (never released)\n- Time going backward → underflow detection, integrity warnings\n\n### 6.3 Work Estimator (request/width.go)\n\nRequest work is estimated by pluggable `WorkEstimatorFunc`:\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimatorFunc func(*http.Request, flowSchemaName, priorityLevelName string) WorkEstimate\n```\n\n**Extensions (already in codebase):**\n- `listWorkEstimator`: Estimates based on object count (calls statsGetter)\n- `mutatingWorkEstimator`: Estimates based on watcher count (calls watchCountGetter)\n- Fallback: Default 1 seat for unknown request types\n\n**Customization hooks:**\n```go\nmaxSeatsFunc := func(priorityLevelName string) uint64 { ... }\nstatsGetter := func(resourceName string) (storage.Stats, error) { ... }\nwatchCountGetter := func(requestInfo *RequestInfo) int { ... }\n```\n\n**Risk:**\n- Overestimating work → false seat exhaustion, unnecessary queueing\n- Underestimating work → true overload with poor fairness\n- Non-deterministic estimates → unpredictable fairness\n\n### 6.4 Shuffle Sharding Dealer (shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go)\n\nShuffle sharding hand selection is delegated to `shufflesharding.Dealer`:\n\n```go\ntype Dealer interface {\n  DealIntoHand(hashValue uint64, backHand []int) []int\n}\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Custom hand-dealing algorithms for:\n- Weighted sharding (some queues get larger hands)\n- Topology-aware sharding (prefer low-latency queues)\n- Adaptive hand sizing (adjust based on collision rates)\n\n**Risk:** Collisions in hand assignment can cause starvation if multiple flows map to same queue.\n\n### 6.5 Metrics Observability (metrics.go)\n\nAll state changes are reported to metrics:\n\n```go\nmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(ctx, qsName, fsName, delta)\nmetrics.AddSeatsInQueues(ctx, qsName, fsName, delta)\nmetrics.SetDispatchMetrics(qsName, currentR, nextDispatchR, ...)\nmetrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qsName, success)\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Hook metrics subsystem to:\n- Export to custom monitoring backend (Prometheus, CloudMonitoring)\n- Trigger alerts on fairness violations\n- Log detailed dispatch decisions\n\n**Risk:** Metrics callback errors will not cause rejection, but may slow down hot paths.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications: Performance, Reliability, and Maintainability\n\n### 7.1 Concurrency and Locking Strategy\n\n**Lock design:**\n- Single `sync.Mutex` per queueset protects all mutable state\n- Lock held during:\n  - Initial request ingress (StartRequest)\n  - Virtual time updates (syncTimeLocked)\n  - All dispatch operations\n  - Request finish handling\n\n**Lock release:**\n- Lock released immediately after decision is made\n- Actual request execution runs outside lock\n- Decision delivery (promise.Get) doesn't hold lock\n\n**Performance implications:**\n```\nLock contention = (arrival rate) × (average time in critical section)\n\nTypical: ~1μs per StartRequest + ~100ns per syncTimeLocked\n         With 10k req/s: ~10ms contention per second (acceptable)\n\nWorst case: Large queuesets (100+ queues) with high arrival rates\n            Round-robin dispatch loop scales O(queues) per dispatch\n            With 1000 queues: ~5μs per dispatch\n```\n\n**Mitigation:** Lock-free data structures for queue peeking (future work).\n\n### 7.2 Memory Footprint\n\nPer queueset:\n- `queueSet` struct: ~500 bytes\n- Per queue: ~200 bytes (FIFO list, sync.Set)\n- Per request: ~256 bytes (context, metadata, promise)\n\n**Example:** 100 queues + 1000 waiting requests = 100×200 + 1000×256 = ~280KB\n\n**Scalability:** Memory grows with O(queues + waiting requests). No inherent limits; configured via QueueLengthLimit.\n\n### 7.3 Virtual Time Stability\n\n**Risk:** Overflow, underflow, or monotonicity violations can corrupt fairness.\n\n**Safeguards:**\n1. **Epoch advancement:** Detects overflow, logs warnings if underflow occurs during decrement\n2. **Monotonicity checks:** `boundNextDispatchLocked` asserts `nextDispatchR >= arrivalR`\n3. **Metrics correlation:** Dispatch metrics include virtual time (external monitoring can alert)\n\n**Operational alert:** If `epoch_advance_errors` > 0, investigate virtual time corruption.\n\n### 7.4 Tuning Parameters and Trade-offs\n\n| Parameter | Location | Impact | Notes |\n|-----------|----------|--------|-------|\n| `DesiredNumQueues` | QueuingConfig | Fairness, latency | Higher → better fairness, higher overhead |\n| `HandSize` | QueuingConfig | Collision, predictability | Higher → lower collision, higher shuffle cost |\n| `QueueLengthLimit` | QueuingConfig | Memory, rejection rate | Higher → more memory, less rejection |\n| `ConcurrencyLimit` | DispatchingConfig | Throughput, latency | Sweet spot depends on hardware |\n| `EstimatedServiceDuration` | queueset.go:215 | Seat allocation fairness | Too high → underutilization; too low → overload |\n\n### 7.5 Observability Checklist\n\n**Key metrics to monitor:**\n1. **`apiserver_priority_level_request_utilization`**: Executing requests / limit (target: 0.7–0.9)\n2. **`apiserver_priority_level_seat_utilization`**: Occupied seats / limit (target: 0.6–0.8)\n3. **`apiserver_priority_level_request_wait_duration`**: P50, P99 queueing latency\n4. **`apiserver_request_total` with `code=429`**: Rejected requests (trending up = concern)\n5. **`apiserver_priority_level_queued_requests`**: Requests waiting (should be < QueueLengthLimit × DesiredNumQueues / 2)\n6. **`apiserver_priority_level_epoch_advance_total`**: Epoch advancements (OK to see every 1–10 seconds under load)\n7. **`apiserver_flowschema_dispatched_requests_total`**: By flow schema (check for fairness across flows)\n\n### 7.6 Debugging and Introspection\n\n**Available methods:**\n- `queueSet.Dump(includeRequestDetails bool)`: Snapshots internal state (lock held during snapshot)\n  - Returns requests in queues, executing requests, virtual times, seat counts\n  - Safe for live queries (not async)\n\n**Limitations:**\n- Dump is point-in-time; state changes immediately after\n- No time-series; must sample repeatedly\n- Expensive for large request counts (O(requests) to snapshot)\n\n**Debug endpoints:**\n- `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/`: Exposes queueset dump via HTTP (if installed)\n\n**Manual troubleshooting:**\n```bash\n# Check if QueueSet is overloaded\ncurl http://localhost:6443/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_queues\n# High: totRequestsWaiting, high: seatsInUse / ConcurrencyLimit\n\n# Check if shuffle sharding is unbalanced\njq '.queues[] | {queue: .index, waiting: (.requests | length), executing}' < dump.json\n# Unbalanced queue lengths indicate collision issues\n\n# Check virtual time advancement\ncurl ... | jq '.queues[] | .nextDispatchR'\n# Should be in ascending order (monotonic); gaps indicate idle queues\n```\n\n### 7.7 Failure Scenarios and Recovery\n\n| Scenario | Symptom | Cause | Recovery |\n|----------|---------|-------|----------|\n| Request stuck waiting | P99 latency spike, single request doesn't finish | Context timeout or handler crash | Request context timeout will trigger cancellation |\n| Queue length limit hit | Requests rejected with 429 | Load > ConcurrencyLimit × DesiredNumQueues / QueueLengthLimit | Reduce load or increase limits |\n| Virtual time overflow | `epoch_advance` warnings in logs | Continuous overload for weeks | Restart API server (resets R) or increase epoch threshold |\n| Memory leak | RAM usage grows unbounded | Requests not calling Finish() | Operator must restart affected server |\n| Unfair dispatch | One flow dominates execution | Hand collision or work estimation error | Check metrics, adjust HandSize or estimator |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Architecture Map: Critical Files and Their Responsibilities\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n├── fairqueuing/\n│   ├── interface.go                    # QueueSet, Request, Config interfaces\n│   ├── queueset/\n│   │   ├── queueset.go                 # Main logic: StartRequest, dispatch, virtual time\n│   │   ├── types.go                    # request, queue, queueSum structs\n│   │   ├── fifo_list.go                # requestFIFO: O(1) queue with running sums\n│   │   ├── queueset_test.go            # fairness and fairness validation\n│   │   └── fifo_list_test.go\n│   ├── eventclock/                     # eventclock.Interface for time operations\n│   └── promise/                        # promise.WriteOnce for deferred decisions\n│\n├── request/\n│   ├── width.go                        # WorkEstimate, WorkEstimatorFunc\n│   ├── seat_seconds.go                 # SeatSeconds: fixed-point work metric\n│   ├── list_work_estimator.go          # Per-list-size work estimation\n│   └── mutating_work_estimator.go      # Per-watcher work estimation\n│\n├── apf_controller.go                   # Main controller: config syncing, priority level state\n├── apf_filter.go                       # Request entry point: Handle(), dispatcher\n├── apf_controller_debug.go             # Debug endpoints\n├── metrics/\n│   └── metrics.go                      # Metrics recording: requests, seats, latencies\n└── debug/\n    └── ...                             # Dump structures and HTTP debug handler\n\nk8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/\n├── shufflesharding.go                  # Dealer: shuffle-sharded hand allocation\n└── shufflesharding_test.go\n```\n\n**Key entry points:**\n1. **`apf_filter.go: Handle()`** → Called by HTTP handler for each request\n2. **`apf_controller.go: startRequest()`** → Routes to QueueSet.StartRequest()\n3. **`queueset.go: StartRequest()`** → Main ingress; enqueues and dispatches\n4. **`queueset.go: dispatchLocked()`** → Fair queue selection and virtual time advancement\n5. **`request.Finish()`** → Client callback; calls queueSet.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n\n---\n\n## 9. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet is a sophisticated fair-queuing implementation adapted for multi-phase request execution and work-aware concurrency control. Its fairness guarantees rest on:\n\n1. **Virtual time scheduling** (fair queuing algorithm)\n2. **Dynamic rate adaptation** (proportional to concurrency limit and queue count)\n3. **Shuffle sharding** (load balancing and collision resistance)\n4. **Work estimation** (seat-seconds accounting)\n5. **Anti-windup mechanisms** (preventing unfair idle-queue priority)\n\n**Strengths:**\n- Provably fair under steady-state assumptions\n- Handles variable request widths (multi-phase execution)\n- Adaptive to load (virtual time rate adjusts)\n- Configurable fairness/performance tradeoff (queue count, hand size)\n\n**Limitations:**\n- Single global lock (contention under extreme load)\n- Fixed work estimator (errors compound across calls)\n- Virtual time is local per queueset (no global fairness across priority levels)\n- Anti-windup is conservative (may allow unfair idle-queue recovery)\n\n**Operational key:** Monitor seat utilization, queue lengths, and dispatch latencies. Tune `DesiredNumQueues` and `ConcurrencyLimit` based on workload characteristics and fairness objectives.\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n- **KEP-1040:** https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n- **Fair Queuing Algorithm (original):** Demers, Keshav, Shenker, \"Analysis and Simulation of a Fair Queueing Algorithm\" (1989)\n- **Shuffle Sharding:** https://dl.acm.org/doi/10.1145/1400519.1400529 (Cushman et al., SIGCOMM 2008)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3433,"cache_read_input_tokens":64231,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3433},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"74f2f4f5-469d-443e-8003-bb09a799d67e","uuid":"0f918d2e-c0b5-41af-b40f-96b0e3dc3636"}

It provides weighted fairness guarantees through virtual time scheduling, shuffle-sharded queue assignment, and adaptive dispatch based on estimated work (seat-seconds). This document traces the end-to-end control flow, dissects the fairness algorithm, and discusses operational tradeoffs.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### 1.1 Purpose\n\nThe QueueSet is the **execution scheduling engine** of API Priority and Fairness (APF). It sits between the APF filter (which classifies requests) and the main request handler (which executes them). Its role:\n\n- **Admission control**: Reject or queue requests when concurrency limits are exceeded\n- **Fair dispatch**: Select which queued request executes next, ensuring:\n  - Proportional fairness among flows (via virtual time)\n  - Starvation prevention (via round-robin queue selection)\n  - Work-aware scheduling (via seat-seconds, not just request count)\n- **Concurrency accounting**: Track occupied \"seats\" (a logical concurrency unit) across phases of request execution\n\n### 1.2 Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n- **APF Controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`): Provides `QueuingConfig` (desired number of queues, queue length limit, hand size for shuffle sharding) and `DispatchingConfig` (concurrency limit)\n- **Request classifiers**: Extract flow distinguisher and match requests to priority levels\n- **Work estimators** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go`): Estimate request width (initial seats, final seats, additional latency) based on request type and payload size\n\n**Downstream dependencies:**\n- **HTTP handler**: Calls `StartRequest()`, then `req.Finish()` when done\n- **Metrics subsystem** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics/`): Observes request counts, seat occupancy, dispatch latencies, rejections\n- **Event clock** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/`): Provides virtual time ticking and delayed event scheduling\n\n### 1.3 Key Data Dependencies\n\n- **WorkEstimate**: Carries `InitialSeats` (concurrency during main phase), `FinalSeats` (reserved after execution), and `AdditionalLatency` (padding duration)\n- **SeatSeconds**: Fixed-point representation of work = seats × duration, with 1e8 internal scale factor\n- **QueuingConfig**: Encodes desired number of queues (0 = bypass queueing, negative = exempt), queue length limit, shuffle-sharding hand size\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Types\n\n#### `queueSet` (queueset.go:85–167)\nThe main orchestrator. Fields include:\n- **`queues []*queue`**: Array of FIFO queues, allocated per shuffle-sharded flow\n- **`currentR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Global virtual time progress meter (R from fair queuing)\n- **`lock sync.Mutex`**: Protects all mutable state\n- **`totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`**: Aggregate seat occupancy\n- **`totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`**: Request counts for metrics\n- **`dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig`**: Concurrency limits and seat accounting denominators\n- **`promiseFactory`**: Creates decision promises (deferred-write channels for async dispatch decisions)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Initial request ingress and rejection (via `StartRequest()`)\n- Virtual time progression and epoch management\n- Dispatch loop orchestration\n- Request completion tracking and seat release\n\n#### `queue` (types.go:93–110)\nPer-flow-distinguisher queue. Fields:\n- **`requestsWaiting fifo`**: Ordered list of queued requests\n- **`requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]`**: Executing requests from this queue (for seat tracking)\n- **`nextDispatchR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Virtual finish time of next dispatch from this queue\n- **`seatsInUse int`**: Occupied seats in this queue\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- FIFO ordering of requests awaiting dispatch\n- Virtual time tracking per queue (anti-windup mechanism)\n\n#### `request` (types.go:33–83)\nRequest wrapper with scheduling metadata. Fields:\n- **`decision promise.WriteOnce`**: Deferred decision (execute/cancel)\n- **`arrivalTime`, `startTime`**: Real timestamps for latency metrics\n- **`arrivalR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Virtual time at arrival\n- **`workEstimate completedWorkEstimate`**: Computed total work (initial + final)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Carries request context and work estimate\n- Defers dispatch decision via promise pattern (allows async decision-setting under lock, decision-reading without lock)\n\n#### `requestFIFO` (fifo_list.go:71–156)\nLinked-list FIFO with aggregate statistics. Methods:\n- **`Enqueue(req)`**: Returns `removeFromFIFOFunc` for O(1) removal\n- **`QueueSum()`**: Returns aggregated `InitialSeatsSum`, `MaxSeatsSum`, `TotalWorkSum`\n- **`Walk(func)`**: Iterates without copying (permits removal during iteration)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- O(1) enqueue/dequeue/remove operations\n- Maintains running sums of seated widths for shuffle-sharding decisions\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Request Arrival: `StartRequest()` (queueset.go:308–356)\n\n```\n┌─ StartRequest(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, ...)\n│\n├─ Step 0: Check if queueing is bypassed\n│  │  (DesiredNumQueues < 1 → concurrency-only mode)\n│  │\n│  ├─ If queues disabled:\n│  │  └─ Call canAccommodateSeatsLocked(workEstimate.MaxSeats)\n│  │     ├─ If yes: dispatchSansQueueLocked() → return request (immediate exec)\n│  │     └─ If no: increment totRequestsRejected, return (nil, isIdleLocked)\n│  │\n│  └─ If queues enabled: proceed to Step 1\n│\n├─ Step 1: Shuffle-shard and enqueue\n│  │\n│  ├─ shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()\n│  │  │\n│  │  ├─ Call shuffleShardLocked(hashValue)\n│  │  │  │  Uses dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue) to get candidate queues\n│  │  │  │  Selects queue with minimum TotalWorkSum (load-balanced assignment)\n│  │  │  │\n│  │  │  └─ Return queue index\n│  │  │\n│  │  ├─ Create request object with:\n│  │  │  ├─ arrivalTime ← clock.Now()\n│  │  │  ├─ arrivalR ← currentR (current virtual time)\n│  │  │  ├─ decision ← promiseFactory(nil) [decision not yet set]\n│  │  │  └─ workEstimate ← completeWorkEstimate(workEstimate)\n│  │  │\n│  │  ├─ Call rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n│  │  │  │\n│  │  │  ├─ If totSeatsInUse >= concurrencyLimit AND queueLength >= queueLengthLimit:\n│  │  │  │  └─ REJECT (return false)\n│  │  │  │\n│  │  │  └─ Else: enqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n│  │  │     ├─ If queue empty: queue.nextDispatchR ← currentR (initialize virtual start)\n│  │  │     ├─ queue.requestsWaiting.Enqueue(request)\n│  │  │     ├─ totRequestsWaiting++, totSeatsWaiting += request.MaxSeats()\n│  │  │     └─ Metrics: AddRequestsInQueues, AddSeatsInQueues\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ If rejected: return nil\n│  │\n│  └─ If enqueued: proceed to Step 2\n│\n├─ Step 2: Immediate dispatch as much as possible\n│  │\n│  └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n│     │  While totRequestsWaiting > 0 AND totSeatsInUse < concurrencyLimit:\n│     │    └─ dispatchLocked() (see Section 3.2)\n│     │\n│     └─ Executes requests from queues until concurrency limit or no queued requests\n│\n└─ Return (request, false)\n   │  If request is nil: caller should reject\n   │  If request is non-nil: caller must call request.Finish() when done\n```\n\n### 3.2 Dispatch: `dispatchLocked()` and Fair Queue Selection (queueset.go:695–743)\n\nFair Queuing uses **virtual time** to achieve fairness. Key insight: dispatch the request whose virtual *finish time* is earliest, ensuring proportional service allocation.\n\n```\n┌─ dispatchLocked()\n│\n├─ findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n│  │\n│  ├─ Iterate round-robin through queues\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ For each queue with waiting requests:\n│  │     │\n│  │     ├─ Peek oldest request\n│  │     │\n│  │     ├─ Compute currentVirtualFinish:\n│  │     │  │  = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n│  │     │  │\n│  │     │  │  Where totalWork = InitialSeats×EstimatedServiceDuration\n│  │     │  │                     + FinalSeats×AdditionalLatency\n│  │     │  │\n│  │     │  └─ If currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish:\n│  │     │     └─ Record this queue as best candidate\n│  │     │\n│  │     └─ Also track virtual dispatch start (nextDispatchR - estimatedWorkInProgress)\n│  │        for metrics\n│  │\n│  ├─ Check canAccommodateSeatsLocked(selectedRequest.MaxSeats)\n│  │  │\n│  │  ├─ If seats exceed ConcurrencyLimit AND executingRequests > 0:\n│  │  │  │  CANNOT dispatch yet (must wait for current requests to finish)\n│  │  │  │\n│  │  │  └─ Return (nil, nil) → caller stops dispatching\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ If can accommodate: dequeue from requestsWaiting\n│  │\n│  ├─ Adjust final seats if they exceed concurrency limit\n│  │  │  (preserve total work by adjusting additional latency)\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ Update round-robin index to start from selected queue next time\n│  │\n│  └─ Return (selectedQueue, selectedRequest)\n│\n├─ Remove request from waiting list:\n│  │  ├─ totRequestsWaiting--, totSeatsWaiting -= request.MaxSeats()\n│  │  ├─ Metrics: AddRequestsInQueues(-1), AddSeatsInQueues(-maxSeats)\n│  │  └─ request.NoteQueued(false)\n│  │\n│  └─ defer boundNextDispatchLocked(queue) [anti-windup; see 3.5]\n│\n├─ Set dispatch decision:\n│  │\n│  └─ If request.decision.Set(decisionExecute) succeeds:\n│     │  (decision promise was unfulfilled; now fulfilled)\n│     │\n│     ├─ Move from waiting to executing:\n│     │  ├─ request.startTime ← clock.Now()\n│     │  ├─ queue.requestsExecuting.Insert(request)\n│     │  ├─ queue.seatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n│     │  ├─ totRequestsExecuting++, totSeatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n│     │  └─ Metrics: AddRequestsExecuting(+1), AddSeatConcurrencyInUse(+seats)\n│     │\n│     ├─ Advance virtual finish time:\n│     │  │\n│     │  └─ queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n│     │     │  \"Cost\" of this request in virtual time\n│     │     │  Larger work → larger virtual advance → less priority to future requests\n│     │     │\n│     │     └─ Other queues see this queue recede in virtual time\n│     │\n│     └─ Return true (dispatch succeeded)\n│\n└─ Return false (if decision.Set failed or no queue candidate)\n   │  Caller will retry this request once another finishes\n   │\n   └─ (Can only happen if request's context was canceled before dispatch)\n```\n\n### 3.3 Virtual Time Progression: `syncTimeLocked()` (queueset.go:465–522)\n\nVirtual time advances proportionally to concurrency limits and active queue load:\n\n```\n┌─ syncTimeLocked(ctx)\n│\n├─ Measure elapsed real time:\n│  │  realNow := clock.Now()\n│  │  timeSinceLast := realNow - lastRealTime\n│  │\n│  └─ lastRealTime ← realNow\n│\n├─ Compute virtual time advancement rate:\n│  │\n│  └─ getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()\n│     │\n│     ├─ activeQueues ← count of non-empty queues\n│     │\n│     ├─ seatsRequested ← ∑(queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.MaxSeatsSum)\n│     │\n│     ├─ If activeQueues == 0:\n│     │  │  return 0 (no advancement while idle)\n│     │  │\n│     │  └─ No virtual time consumption\n│     │\n│     └─ Else:\n│        return min(seatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n│        │\n│        │  Each active queue \"consumes\" an equal share of concurrency\n│        │  Unmet demand (seatsRequested > limit) means queues share fairly\n│        │  Unmet demand (seatsRequested < limit) means virtual time = real time\n│\n├─ Advance global progress meter:\n│  │\n│  └─ currentR += SeatsTimesDuration(ratio, timeSinceLast)\n│     │  Converts: (seats/queue) × (elapsed time) → seat-seconds\n│     │  Uses fixed-point SeatSeconds (scale = 1e8)\n│\n└─ If currentR >= highR (overflow threshold):\n   │\n   └─ advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n      │  Decrement currentR and all queue.nextDispatchR by rDecrement (2^63)\n      │  Prevents uint64 overflow\n      │  Idempotent for queues that become empty\n      │\n      └─ [See Section 3.5 for anti-windup implications]\n```\n\n**Key insight:** Virtual time rate is `(fair share of concurrency) / (queue count)`. If 4 queues compete for 100-seat limit, each queue \"time\" advances at 25 seats/sec in real time, regardless of actual demand. This provides proportional fairness.\n\n### 3.4 Request Completion: `finishRequestLocked()` (queueset.go:863–943)\n\n```\n┌─ finishRequestLocked(req)\n│\n├─ Update counters:\n│  │  ├─ totRequestsExecuting--\n│  │  ├─ Metrics: AddRequestsExecuting(-1)\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ actualServiceDuration := now - req.startTime\n│\n├─ Determine seat release timing:\n│  │\n│  └─ If AdditionalLatency <= 0:\n│     │  Release all seats immediately\n│     │\n│     └─ releaseSeatsLocked():\n│        ├─ totSeatsInUse -= req.MaxSeats()\n│        ├─ req.queue.seatsInUse -= req.MaxSeats()\n│        ├─ Metrics: AddSeatConcurrencyInUse(-seats)\n│        └─ Call removeQueueIfEmptyLocked() [queue housekeeping]\n│\n│  Else:\n│     │\n│     ├─ Release InitialSeats immediately\n│     │\n│     ├─ Schedule deferred release of FinalSeats after AdditionalLatency\n│     │  │  via clock.EventAfterDuration(func() { releaseSeatsLocked() }, AdditionalLatency)\n│     │  │\n│     │  └─ Client perceives no latency; seats held invisibly in background\n│     │\n│     └─ Post-release: dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n│\n├─ Adjust queue's virtual start time (anti-windup):\n│  │\n│  └─ If req was dispatched from a queue:\n│     │\n│     └─ queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(req.InitialSeats,\n│        EstimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n│        │\n│        │  Rationale:\n│        │  - Estimated cost: initialSeats × estimatedServiceDuration\n│        │  - Actual cost: initialSeats × actualServiceDuration\n│        │  - Difference: credit back to queue if actual < estimated\n│        │\n│        └─ Reduces queue's virtual start time → increases dispatch priority\n│\n└─ Remove request from queue:\n   │\n   ├─ If queued: queue.requestsExecuting.Delete(req)\n   │\n   └─ If not queued (concurrency-only mode):\n      └─ requestsExecutingSet.Delete(req)\n```\n\n### 3.5 Anti-Windup: `boundNextDispatchLocked()` (queueset.go:952–964)\n\n**Problem:** A queue that cannot use all its allocated concurrency (e.g., bursty single-stream) accumulates a decreasing virtual start time (its `nextDispatchR`), gaining unfair priority over busier queues. The anti-windup bounds this:\n\n```\n┌─ boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n│\n├─ If queue is now empty: return (no action needed)\n│\n├─ Peek oldest waiting request:\n│  │  oldestReqFromMinQueue := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n│  │\n│  └─ virtualStartBound := oldestReqFromMinQueue.arrivalR\n│     │  (request cannot start before it arrives)\n│\n└─ If queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound:\n   │\n   ├─ queue.nextDispatchR ← virtualStartBound\n   │\n   └─ Log: \"AntiWindup tweaked queue\" with delta\n      │\n      └─ Prevents dispatch before arrival\n```\n\n**Rationale:** If a queue is idle (no requests), its virtual time would advance unbounded. When a new request arrives, we clamp the queue's virtual start ≥ arrival time. This prevents \"catching up\" too much.\n\n### 3.6 Request Waiting and Decision: `request.wait()` (queueset.go:397–441)\n\n```\n┌─ req.wait() [called by req.Finish() to get dispatch decision]\n│\n├─ Fetch decision promise:\n│  │  decisionAny := req.decision.Get()\n│  │  │  Blocks until decision is fulfilled (by dispatchLocked or timeout)\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ Lock queueset and sync virtual time\n│\n├─ If decision == decisionExecute:\n│  │  return (true, false)  ← execute the request\n│  │\n│  └─ Caller's execFn() will run immediately\n│\n├─ Else (decision == decisionCancel, due to context timeout/cancel):\n│  │\n│  ├─ Remove request from queue:\n│  │  │  queue.requestsWaiting.Length()--\n│  │  │  totSeatsWaiting -= req.MaxSeats()\n│  │  │\n│  │  └─ Metrics: AddReject(..., \"time-out\")\n│  │\n│  └─ return (false, isIdleLocked())  ← request was rejected (timed out)\n│\n└─ Note: Cannot call wait() twice on same request (enforced)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Fairness Algorithm Details\n\n### 4.1 Fair Queuing Foundations\n\nThe QueueSet implements a variant of **Weighted Fair Queuing (WFQ)**. The key idea:\n\n1. **Virtual Time (R):** A monotonically increasing counter measuring work allocated\n2. **Virtual Start/Finish:** Each request has a virtual arrival time (`arrivalR`) and virtual finish time (`arrivalR + totalWork`)\n3. **Selection Rule:** Always dispatch the request with minimum virtual finish time\n4. **Guarantee:** Over long timescales, each flow receives service proportional to its demand (up to fair share)\n\n**Example:**\n- Request A: work = 10 seat-seconds, arrives at R=0 → finishes at R=10\n- Request B: work = 20 seat-seconds, arrives at R=0 → finishes at R=20\n- Dispatch order: A (finish@10), then B (finish@20)\n- If another A arrives at R=10: A2 finishes at R=20 (same as B)\n- Fair: both flows receive equal service time\n\n### 4.2 Virtual Time Rate Adaptation\n\nInstead of fixed-weight fair queuing, the QueueSet uses **dynamic virtual time progression** based on concurrency limits and load:\n\n```\nvirtual_time_rate = min(seatsRequested, concurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\n**Implications:**\n\n| Scenario | seatsRequested | activeQueues | Rate per Queue |\n|----------|----------------|--------------|----------------|\n| 4 queues, 100 seats | 100 | 4 | 25 seats/sec |\n| 4 queues, 40 seats | 40 | 4 | 10 seats/sec |\n| 4 queues, 200 seats | 200 | 4 | 25 seats/sec (clamped) |\n| 2 queues, 100 seats | 100 | 2 | 50 seats/sec |\n\n**Effect:** Queues with low demand don't slow down others. Queues sharing the limit get equal virtual time.\n\n### 4.3 Work Estimation and Seat-Seconds\n\nWork is measured in **seat-seconds**, a two-phase model:\n\n```\ntotalWork = InitialSeats × EstimatedServiceDuration\n          + FinalSeats × AdditionalLatency\n\nExample:\n  ListRequest with 1000 objects\n  InitialSeats=3, EstimatedServiceDuration=3ms → 9ms-seats\n  FinalSeats=1, AdditionalLatency=0 → 0ms-seats\n  Total work = 9 ms-seats\n```\n\n**Why two phases?**\n- **Initial phase:** Request actively uses concurrency (network send, compute)\n- **Final phase:** Minimal active use; seats held for flow completion guarantees (e.g., TCP RST handling)\n\n### 4.4 Shuffle Sharding: Load Balancing Among Queues\n\nShuffle sharding solves a crucial problem: **head-of-line blocking**. Without it, a single slow request from flow X blocks all other requests from X.\n\n**Algorithm** (shuffleShardLocked, queueset.go:583–612):\n\n```\n1. dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, handSize)\n   │  Input: flow's hash, desired hand size (e.g., 8)\n   │  Output: array of queue indices (e.g., [3, 7, 1, 5, 2, 8, 0, 4])\n   │\n   │  Ensures: different flows get different hands, but hands overlap\n   │           (reduces collision probability vs. simple hash mod)\n\n2. Iterate through hand, selecting queue with minimum TotalWorkSum\n   │  offset := enqueues % handSize  (round-robin offset for fairness)\n   │  For i = 0 to handSize-1:\n   │    queueIdx := hand[(offset + i) % handSize]\n   │    if queueSum[queueIdx].TotalWorkSum < minQueueWorkSum:\n   │      bestQueueIdx ← queueIdx\n\n3. Enqueue into bestQueueIdx\n\nOutcome:\n  - Same flow always gets queued to one of its hand's queues\n  - Requests from different flows spread across queues\n  - Load balancing: pick least-loaded queue from hand\n  - Starvation prevention: offset ensures round-robin fairness among hand members\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Shuffle sharding trades determinism for fairness. A flow may experience variable queueing if its hand happens to be congested.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Overflow Management\n\n**Problem:** Virtual time `R` is a `uint64`. After ~584 CPU-years of continuous operation, it overflows.\n\n**Solution:** Epoch advancement (advanceEpoch, queueset.go:492–522)\n\n```\nTrigger: currentR >= highR (where highR = 2^63 + 2^62)\n\nAction:\n  1. Subtract rDecrement (2^63) from:\n     - currentR\n     - All queue.nextDispatchR\n     - All request.arrivalR (for queued requests)\n\n  2. Log the event with old/new values and integrity check\n\nRationale:\n  - Preserves relative ordering (A - C == (A-D) - (C-D))\n  - Resets counter, extending lifetime to another ~584 years\n  - Idempotent for empty queues (nextDispatchR → 0 if queue unused)\n```\n\n**Risk:** If any adjustment underflows (detected and logged), fairness metrics become unreliable, but scheduling continues.\n\n### 5.2 Seat Accommodation and Borrowing Limits\n\n**Problem:** A request may require more seats than the concurrency limit.\n\n**Handling** (canAccommodateSeatsLocked, queueset.go:748–769):\n\n```\nCase 1: DesiredNumQueues < 0 (exempt from limitation)\n  → Always return true (admit request immediately)\n\nCase 2: RequestSeats > ConcurrencyLimit\n  → If totRequestsExecuting == 0: admit (allow one to start)\n  → Else: reject (wait for current requests to finish)\n\nCase 3: RequestSeats + TotSeatsInUse <= ConcurrencyLimit\n  → Admit (sufficient capacity)\n\nCase 4: RequestSeats + TotSeatsInUse > ConcurrencyLimit\n  → Reject (insufficient capacity, must wait)\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Case 2 allows a single request to exceed the limit, but prevents cascading overflow. This violates strict concurrency control but ensures liveness.\n\n### 5.3 Virtual Dispatch Start (Anti-Windup) Limitations\n\n**Problem:** A queue that alternates between idle and active can accumulate a very early `nextDispatchR`, gaining unfair priority.\n\n**Partial mitigation:** boundNextDispatchLocked bounds `nextDispatchR ≥ oldestWaitingRequest.arrivalR`.\n\n**Limitation:** This bound is conservative. If a queue is idle for 1 hour, then receives a request, its virtual start is bumped to the current virtual time, but by then global virtual time has advanced ~10^6 seat-seconds. The queue may have gained priority unfairly.\n\n**Why not fully resync?** Setting `nextDispatchR = currentR` for each idle queue would be too aggressive, allowing \"fresh\" queues to cut in line.\n\n### 5.4 Queue Attrition and Configuration Changes\n\n**Problem:** If desired number of queues decreases, we can't immediately remove occupied queues.\n\n**Handling** (setConfiguration, queueset.go:254–287):\n\n```\nIf DesiredNumQueues decreases from 10 to 5:\n  1. Do not remove extra queues immediately\n  2. Only remove queues when they become empty (attrition)\n  3. Other queue parameters (QueueLengthLimit) frozen while removing queues\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Transient over-provisioning until queues drain. Memory impact is bounded by queue count (each queue is ~200 bytes) and request count.\n\n### 5.5 Queue Length Limits and Rejection\n\n**Rejection criteria** (rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked, queueset.go:618–629):\n\n```\nReject if:\n  totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND\n  curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit\n\nRationale:\n  - Prevent unbounded queue growth (memory DOS)\n  - Allow queueing when concurrency is available (latency isolation)\n  - Admit if either constraint has room\n```\n\n**Problem:** This is an AND condition, not OR. If concurrency limit is hit but queue is short, request is admitted. If queue is full but concurrency available, request is admitted. Only when both are maxed is it rejected.\n\n**Justification:** Reduces unfair rejection during transient overload.\n\n### 5.6 Estimation Error and Service Time Feedback\n\n**Problem:** `EstimatedServiceDuration` is fixed (default 3ms) per queueset. Actual service times vary widely.\n\n**Feedback mechanism** (finishRequestLocked, queueset.go:937–938):\n\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(req.InitialSeats,\n                                           estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n```\n\n**Effect:** If actual < estimated, queue's virtual start decreases (gains priority). If actual > estimated, increases (loses priority).\n\n**Limitation:** Feedback is local to queue; a flow's error doesn't propagate to other queues in the hand. Flow-wide fairness can degrade if one queue overestimates.\n\n### 5.7 Metrics Observation Lag\n\n**Race:** Metrics are updated under lock, but observed external to lock. Between observation and action, state may change.\n\n**Accepted:** This is inherent to sampling metrics. APF clients should not act on single observations.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 6.1 Promise Factory (queueset.go:47–54)\n\nThe dispatch decision is encapsulated in a `promise.WriteOnce` (write-once channel with context cancellation).\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n\nordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory returns promise.NewWriteOnce\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Replace with custom promise implementation for:\n- Custom cancellation behavior (e.g., explicit ack before canceling)\n- Observability (log all decisions)\n- Testing (deterministic decision injection)\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect promise semantics can cause:\n- Deadlock if Set blocks\n- Data races if not thread-safe\n- Request leaks if decision never set\n\n### 6.2 Clock and Virtual Time Control (eventclock.Interface)\n\nQueueSet accepts an `eventclock.Interface` for time operations:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n  Now() time.Time\n  EventAfterDuration(func(time.Time), time.Duration)\n  ...\n}\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Inject custom clock for:\n- **Testing:** Mock time, fast-forward virtual time\n- **Simulation:** Custom virtual time rates\n- **Observability:** Instrument all time-related decisions\n\n**Risk:**\n- Incorrect `EventAfterDuration` timing → seat leaks (never released)\n- Time going backward → underflow detection, integrity warnings\n\n### 6.3 Work Estimator (request/width.go)\n\nRequest work is estimated by pluggable `WorkEstimatorFunc`:\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimatorFunc func(*http.Request, flowSchemaName, priorityLevelName string) WorkEstimate\n```\n\n**Extensions (already in codebase):**\n- `listWorkEstimator`: Estimates based on object count (calls statsGetter)\n- `mutatingWorkEstimator`: Estimates based on watcher count (calls watchCountGetter)\n- Fallback: Default 1 seat for unknown request types\n\n**Customization hooks:**\n```go\nmaxSeatsFunc := func(priorityLevelName string) uint64 { ... }\nstatsGetter := func(resourceName string) (storage.Stats, error) { ... }\nwatchCountGetter := func(requestInfo *RequestInfo) int { ... }\n```\n\n**Risk:**\n- Overestimating work → false seat exhaustion, unnecessary queueing\n- Underestimating work → true overload with poor fairness\n- Non-deterministic estimates → unpredictable fairness\n\n### 6.4 Shuffle Sharding Dealer (shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go)\n\nShuffle sharding hand selection is delegated to `shufflesharding.Dealer`:\n\n```go\ntype Dealer interface {\n  DealIntoHand(hashValue uint64, backHand []int) []int\n}\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Custom hand-dealing algorithms for:\n- Weighted sharding (some queues get larger hands)\n- Topology-aware sharding (prefer low-latency queues)\n- Adaptive hand sizing (adjust based on collision rates)\n\n**Risk:** Collisions in hand assignment can cause starvation if multiple flows map to same queue.\n\n### 6.5 Metrics Observability (metrics.go)\n\nAll state changes are reported to metrics:\n\n```go\nmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(ctx, qsName, fsName, delta)\nmetrics.AddSeatsInQueues(ctx, qsName, fsName, delta)\nmetrics.SetDispatchMetrics(qsName, currentR, nextDispatchR, ...)\nmetrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qsName, success)\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Hook metrics subsystem to:\n- Export to custom monitoring backend (Prometheus, CloudMonitoring)\n- Trigger alerts on fairness violations\n- Log detailed dispatch decisions\n\n**Risk:** Metrics callback errors will not cause rejection, but may slow down hot paths.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications: Performance, Reliability, and Maintainability\n\n### 7.1 Concurrency and Locking Strategy\n\n**Lock design:**\n- Single `sync.Mutex` per queueset protects all mutable state\n- Lock held during:\n  - Initial request ingress (StartRequest)\n  - Virtual time updates (syncTimeLocked)\n  - All dispatch operations\n  - Request finish handling\n\n**Lock release:**\n- Lock released immediately after decision is made\n- Actual request execution runs outside lock\n- Decision delivery (promise.Get) doesn't hold lock\n\n**Performance implications:**\n```\nLock contention = (arrival rate) × (average time in critical section)\n\nTypical: ~1μs per StartRequest + ~100ns per syncTimeLocked\n         With 10k req/s: ~10ms contention per second (acceptable)\n\nWorst case: Large queuesets (100+ queues) with high arrival rates\n            Round-robin dispatch loop scales O(queues) per dispatch\n            With 1000 queues: ~5μs per dispatch\n```\n\n**Mitigation:** Lock-free data structures for queue peeking (future work).\n\n### 7.2 Memory Footprint\n\nPer queueset:\n- `queueSet` struct: ~500 bytes\n- Per queue: ~200 bytes (FIFO list, sync.Set)\n- Per request: ~256 bytes (context, metadata, promise)\n\n**Example:** 100 queues + 1000 waiting requests = 100×200 + 1000×256 = ~280KB\n\n**Scalability:** Memory grows with O(queues + waiting requests). No inherent limits; configured via QueueLengthLimit.\n\n### 7.3 Virtual Time Stability\n\n**Risk:** Overflow, underflow, or monotonicity violations can corrupt fairness.\n\n**Safeguards:**\n1. **Epoch advancement:** Detects overflow, logs warnings if underflow occurs during decrement\n2. **Monotonicity checks:** `boundNextDispatchLocked` asserts `nextDispatchR >= arrivalR`\n3. **Metrics correlation:** Dispatch metrics include virtual time (external monitoring can alert)\n\n**Operational alert:** If `epoch_advance_errors` > 0, investigate virtual time corruption.\n\n### 7.4 Tuning Parameters and Trade-offs\n\n| Parameter | Location | Impact | Notes |\n|-----------|----------|--------|-------|\n| `DesiredNumQueues` | QueuingConfig | Fairness, latency | Higher → better fairness, higher overhead |\n| `HandSize` | QueuingConfig | Collision, predictability | Higher → lower collision, higher shuffle cost |\n| `QueueLengthLimit` | QueuingConfig | Memory, rejection rate | Higher → more memory, less rejection |\n| `ConcurrencyLimit` | DispatchingConfig | Throughput, latency | Sweet spot depends on hardware |\n| `EstimatedServiceDuration` | queueset.go:215 | Seat allocation fairness | Too high → underutilization; too low → overload |\n\n### 7.5 Observability Checklist\n\n**Key metrics to monitor:**\n1. **`apiserver_priority_level_request_utilization`**: Executing requests / limit (target: 0.7–0.9)\n2. **`apiserver_priority_level_seat_utilization`**: Occupied seats / limit (target: 0.6–0.8)\n3. **`apiserver_priority_level_request_wait_duration`**: P50, P99 queueing latency\n4. **`apiserver_request_total` with `code=429`**: Rejected requests (trending up = concern)\n5. **`apiserver_priority_level_queued_requests`**: Requests waiting (should be < QueueLengthLimit × DesiredNumQueues / 2)\n6. **`apiserver_priority_level_epoch_advance_total`**: Epoch advancements (OK to see every 1–10 seconds under load)\n7. **`apiserver_flowschema_dispatched_requests_total`**: By flow schema (check for fairness across flows)\n\n### 7.6 Debugging and Introspection\n\n**Available methods:**\n- `queueSet.Dump(includeRequestDetails bool)`: Snapshots internal state (lock held during snapshot)\n  - Returns requests in queues, executing requests, virtual times, seat counts\n  - Safe for live queries (not async)\n\n**Limitations:**\n- Dump is point-in-time; state changes immediately after\n- No time-series; must sample repeatedly\n- Expensive for large request counts (O(requests) to snapshot)\n\n**Debug endpoints:**\n- `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/`: Exposes queueset dump via HTTP (if installed)\n\n**Manual troubleshooting:**\n```bash\n# Check if QueueSet is overloaded\ncurl http://localhost:6443/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_queues\n# High: totRequestsWaiting, high: seatsInUse / ConcurrencyLimit\n\n# Check if shuffle sharding is unbalanced\njq '.queues[] | {queue: .index, waiting: (.requests | length), executing}' < dump.json\n# Unbalanced queue lengths indicate collision issues\n\n# Check virtual time advancement\ncurl ... | jq '.queues[] | .nextDispatchR'\n# Should be in ascending order (monotonic); gaps indicate idle queues\n```\n\n### 7.7 Failure Scenarios and Recovery\n\n| Scenario | Symptom | Cause | Recovery |\n|----------|---------|-------|----------|\n| Request stuck waiting | P99 latency spike, single request doesn't finish | Context timeout or handler crash | Request context timeout will trigger cancellation |\n| Queue length limit hit | Requests rejected with 429 | Load > ConcurrencyLimit × DesiredNumQueues / QueueLengthLimit | Reduce load or increase limits |\n| Virtual time overflow | `epoch_advance` warnings in logs | Continuous overload for weeks | Restart API server (resets R) or increase epoch threshold |\n| Memory leak | RAM usage grows unbounded | Requests not calling Finish() | Operator must restart affected server |\n| Unfair dispatch | One flow dominates execution | Hand collision or work estimation error | Check metrics, adjust HandSize or estimator |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Architecture Map: Critical Files and Their Responsibilities\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n├── fairqueuing/\n│   ├── interface.go                    # QueueSet, Request, Config interfaces\n│   ├── queueset/\n│   │   ├── queueset.go                 # Main logic: StartRequest, dispatch, virtual time\n│   │   ├── types.go                    # request, queue, queueSum structs\n│   │   ├── fifo_list.go                # requestFIFO: O(1) queue with running sums\n│   │   ├── queueset_test.go            # fairness and fairness validation\n│   │   └── fifo_list_test.go\n│   ├── eventclock/                     # eventclock.Interface for time operations\n│   └── promise/                        # promise.WriteOnce for deferred decisions\n│\n├── request/\n│   ├── width.go                        # WorkEstimate, WorkEstimatorFunc\n│   ├── seat_seconds.go                 # SeatSeconds: fixed-point work metric\n│   ├── list_work_estimator.go          # Per-list-size work estimation\n│   └── mutating_work_estimator.go      # Per-watcher work estimation\n│\n├── apf_controller.go                   # Main controller: config syncing, priority level state\n├── apf_filter.go                       # Request entry point: Handle(), dispatcher\n├── apf_controller_debug.go             # Debug endpoints\n├── metrics/\n│   └── metrics.go                      # Metrics recording: requests, seats, latencies\n└── debug/\n    └── ...                             # Dump structures and HTTP debug handler\n\nk8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/\n├── shufflesharding.go                  # Dealer: shuffle-sharded hand allocation\n└── shufflesharding_test.go\n```\n\n**Key entry points:**\n1. **`apf_filter.go: Handle()`** → Called by HTTP handler for each request\n2. **`apf_controller.go: startRequest()`** → Routes to QueueSet.StartRequest()\n3. **`queueset.go: StartRequest()`** → Main ingress; enqueues and dispatches\n4. **`queueset.go: dispatchLocked()`** → Fair queue selection and virtual time advancement\n5. **`request.Finish()`** → Client callback; calls queueSet.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n\n---\n\n## 9. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet is a sophisticated fair-queuing implementation adapted for multi-phase request execution and work-aware concurrency control. Its fairness guarantees rest on:\n\n1. **Virtual time scheduling** (fair queuing algorithm)\n2. **Dynamic rate adaptation** (proportional to concurrency limit and queue count)\n3. **Shuffle sharding** (load balancing and collision resistance)\n4. **Work estimation** (seat-seconds accounting)\n5. **Anti-windup mechanisms** (preventing unfair idle-queue priority)\n\n**Strengths:**\n- Provably fair under steady-state assumptions\n- Handles variable request widths (multi-phase execution)\n- Adaptive to load (virtual time rate adjusts)\n- Configurable fairness/performance tradeoff (queue count, hand size)\n\n**Limitations:**\n- Single global lock (contention under extreme load)\n- Fixed work estimator (errors compound across calls)\n- Virtual time is local per queueset (no global fairness across priority levels)\n- Anti-windup is conservative (may allow unfair idle-queue recovery)\n\n**Operational key:** Monitor seat utilization, queue lengths, and dispatch latencies. Tune `DesiredNumQueues` and `ConcurrencyLimit` based on workload characteristics and fairness objectives.\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n- **KEP-1040:** https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n- **Fair Queuing Algorithm (original):** Demers, Keshav, Shenker, \"Analysis and Simulation of a Fair Queueing Algorithm\" (1989)\n- **Shuffle Sharding:** https://dl.acm.org/doi/10.1145/1400519.1400529 (Cushman et al., SIGCOMM 2008)\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
